#### What this PR does / why we need it:
Bug:
Currently, the MultiKueue admission check (which is required to span all resources of a Cluster Queue)
is applied to workloads inside the Workload Controller when it does not have an admission (quota reservation) ONLY when the CQ's admission checks all cover every resource flavor defined for the CQ (i.e. defined in its Resource Groups).

This leads to an issue described in #7254:

1. We define a CQ on the Manager. It support flavor1 and flavor2. On the CQ we define the MK AC and an additional, custom AC spanning only flavor1.
1. A workload is admitted to the CQ on the Manager and has a Remote Workload Admitted on a Worker Cluster.
1. We loose connection to the Worker, but the Worker is still running. In this case, after enough time the Manager will Backoff the workload and, in the current implementation, remove both ACs, since the custom one does not support all flavors on the CQ.
1. Now if the worker gets reconnected, but the manager workload no longer has the MK AC, we will not process it in the MK Reconciler, meaning the remote workload admitted on the now reconnected Worker will continue running until the AC check is re-added to the WL on the Manager (aka when it gets an admission). All the while the underlying job will continue executing on the Worker. This means it will reserve resources there while manager workload may have proceeded to dispatch to and admit on a different worker in the meantime, causing a double reservation of resources invisible to the Manager.

Fix:
The PR updates the logic assigning/removing admission checks to/from the workload in Workload Controller.
Now, all checks that apply to all resource flavors of a Cluster Queue will be applied to the Workload even before an admission with a flavor is populated, EVEN if other ACs that span only some resources of the CQ are defined.
For the MK AC - this means the check should be applied to all workloads targeting the CQ anointed with one.

#### Which issue(s) this PR fixes:
<!--
*Automatically closes linked issue when PR is merged.
Usage: `Fixes #<issue number>`, or `Fixes (paste link of issue)`.
_If PR is about `failing-tests or flakes`, please post the related issues/tests in a comment and do not use `Fixes`_*
-->
Fixes #7254

#### Special notes for your reviewer:
NONE

#### Does this PR introduce a user-facing change?
<!--
If no, just write "NONE" in the release-note block below.
If yes, a release note is required:
Enter your extended release note in the block below. If the PR requires additional action from users switching to the new release, include the string "action required".
-->
```release-note
AdmissionChecks: fix the bug that on backoff admission checks which are spanning all ResourceFlavors, such as MultiKueue, may be missing in the Workload’s status. 

For MultiKueue that manifested with a bug, when aside from the MultiKueue admission check there was another non-MultiKueue admission check. In the scenario when eviction on the management cluster happened the manager that had temporarily lost connection to a worker, the remote workload would keep running on the reconnected worker, despite the workload staying without reservation on the manager cluster.
```

### Comment by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) — 2026-02-24T09:44:18Z

> Out of curiosity, what is the real world scenario in which MultiKueue is combined with other AdmissionChecks?

Basing it on https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/issues/7254.

1. We define a CQ on the Manager. It support flavor1 and flavor2. On the CQ we define the MK AC and an additional, custom AC spanning only flavor1.
2. A workload is admitted to the CQ on the Manager and has a Remote Workload Admitted on a Worker Cluster.
3. We loose connection to the Worker, but the Worker is still running. In this case, after enough time the Manager will Backoff the workload and, in the current implementation, remove both ACs, since the custom one does not support all flavors on the CQ.
4. Now if the worker gets reconnected, but the manager workload no longer has the MK AC, we will not process it in the MK Reconciler, meaning the remote workload admitted on the now reconnected Worker will continue running until the AC check is re-added to the WL on the Manager (aka when it gets an admission). All the while the underlying job will continue executing on the Worker.


This PR remedies that by ensuring that in the Workload Controller specifically the logic adds/keeps all admission checks that span all resources on the workload, meaning the MK admission check will remain on the WL in this case and the MK Reconciler will ensure the Remote Workload is deleted form the worker since the Manager WL has no quota reservation atm.

### Comment by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) — 2026-02-24T13:02:51Z

> This I understand. The question was more about what other AdmissionChecks make sense together with MK.

I don't have any concrete examples as of right now. I can only speak in general terms.

Given that a user can define custom admission checks with dedicated controllers we can't guarantee no one will ever decide to implement such an AC to further customize how MK behaves for specific resource flavors.

Whether that should be allowed to happen (and if yes - should its current handling remain or be updated) is another matter with its own caveats. Currently:
* Such a check would not affect the dispatch of a workload itself unless it enters the Rejected or Retry state. In fact, the check could remain in the Pending state, keeping the workload on the manager from being admitted (condition admitted), but the quota would be reserved and remotes would be created as usual. This could even lead to the workload finishing without being officially admitted at all. This behavior is not ideal and inconsistent with what an AC is meant to be doing: instead of keeping the workload from admission until Ready, it keeps it from admission only after it is Rejected (or Retrying after rejection).
* Even though the workload can end up finished despite such a check never leaving the Pending state, the check could enter the Rejected or Retry state, leading to the workloads eviction and removal of all of the remote workloads.


If we do not want to handle additional checks on an MK CQ, then a separate PR should be created to adjust the restrictions on Manager Cluster Queues. I added the summary provided here to the bug report: #7254. PTAL and lets discuss there.

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-02-24T16:47:30Z

> This I understand. The question was more about what other AdmissionChecks make sense together with MK.

I think so, but even if we wouldn't see a use-case yet, someone may discover since the AdmissionChecks allow for any external mechanism. So, we should basically conform to the API we allow with validation.

One example we discussed in the context of external ACs is "budgeting". I can imagine someone wants to check the budget at the Manager cluster level, for two reasons:
1. to make the budget check accurate - otherwise it would require the external AC to have some synchronization database reachable from the different clusters
2. to avoid throttling at the worker clusters later in the pipeline

### Comment by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-02-26T10:49:14Z

> I think so, but even if we wouldn't see a use-case yet, someone may discover since the AdmissionChecks allow for any external mechanism. So, we should basically conform to the API we allow with validation.
> One example we discussed in the context of external ACs is "budgeting". 

Maybe this should we handled more explicitly then, because IIUC right now the workload will be replicated to the workers when the quota is reserved without waiting for the checks.

### Comment by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-03-10T14:04:34Z

Comments about the description and release notes:

1. "Admission" != "Quota reservation", at least in terms of our external API language.
    "Set before admission" is a must-be for AdmissionChecks anyway.
    So I'd rather say "before quota reservation".

2. In the release notes, besides the above, I'd also make some shortening changes:

    * _Workloads will be assigned Admission Checks which cover all of a Cluster Queue's Resource Flavors sooner (before **quota is reserved, even before any flavors are assigned**)_.
       And I'd drop the rest of this sentence (which is syntactically complex, took me some time to understand, yet I don't think it brings much value).

    * Instead of describing the "bug scenario", I'd just say
       _Bug scenario: # 7254_
       Or, if you want to offer a more comprehensible summary of the bug (which I guess is your intent):
       _Bug scenario: # 7254 (summarized in the description of # 9359)_
       Or sth like this.

    My intent here is to keep this release note possibly short, to make it easier to grasp.

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-04-08T13:26:33Z

CPs:
- https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/10331
- https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/10332

### Comment by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2026-04-16T11:50:18Z

/release-note-edit
```release-note
AdmissionChecks: Workloads will be assigned Admission Checks, which cover all of a Cluster Queue's Resource Flavors, regardless of if/what flavors were assigned yet. Workloads with empty requests (no flavors assigned in admission) will be treated as requiring all Admission Checks (only affects tests).

In MultiKueue context:
1. Every workload admitted to an MK queue will always be annotated with the MultiKueue admission check.
2. Bug fix: # 7254 (summarized in # 9359) - remote workloads will always be removed from workers when the manager workload looses quota reservation.
```

### Comment by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2026-04-16T11:55:09Z

/release-note-edit

```release-note
MultiKueue: Fixed an issue where the MultiKueue admission check could be removed from a workload that had no quota reservation (e.g. during backoff) if the ClusterQueue also had admission checks 
  covering only some of its resource flavors. When this happened on a manager that had temporarily lost connection to a worker, the remote workload would keep running on the reconnected worker —   
  invisible to the manager — risking double resource reservation.                                                                                                                                    
                                                                                                                                                                                                     
  Admission checks that cover all of a ClusterQueue's resource flavors are now applied to workloads regardless of whether flavors have been assigned, ensuring the MultiKueue check stays attached   
  and remote workloads are reliably reconciled. (#7254)
```

### Comment by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2026-04-16T11:57:23Z

/release-note-edit

```release-note
MultiKueue: Fixed an issue where the MultiKueue admission check could be removed from a workload that had no quota reservation (e.g. during backoff) if the ClusterQueue also had admission checks 
  covering only some of its resource flavors. When this happened on a manager that had temporarily lost connection to a worker, the remote workload would keep running on the reconnected worker —   
  invisible to the manager — risking double resource reservation.                                                                                                                                    
                                                                                                                                                                                                     
  Now, admission checks that cover all of a ClusterQueue's resource flavors are now applied to workloads regardless of whether flavors have been assigned, ensuring the MultiKueue check stays attached   
  and remote workloads are reliably reconciled. (#7254)
```

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-04-16T12:17:47Z

/release-note-edit
```release-note
AdmissionChecks: fix the bug that on backoff admission checks which are spanning all ResourceFlavors, such as MultiKueue, may be missing in the Workload’s status. 

For MultiKueue that manifested with a bug, when aside from the MK admission check there was another non-MultiKueue admission check. In the scenario when eviction on the management cluster happened the manager that had temporarily lost connection to a worker, the remote workload would keep running on the reconnected worker, despite the workload staying without reservation on the manager cluster.
```

### Comment by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2026-04-16T12:22:47Z

/release-note-edit
```release-note
AdmissionChecks: fix the bug that on backoff admission checks which are spanning all ResourceFlavors, such as MultiKueue, may be missing in the Workload’s status. 

For MultiKueue that manifested with a bug, when aside from the MultiKueue admission check there was another non-MultiKueue admission check. In the scenario when eviction on the management cluster happened the manager that had temporarily lost connection to a worker, the remote workload would keep running on the reconnected worker, despite the workload staying without reservation on the manager cluster.
```

## Reviews

### Review by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) (commented) — 2026-02-23T15:57:44Z

I'll do another review pass later, but posting one minor thing already.

Also - I'd consider rewording the release note a little bit. Maybe try to focus on the impact or some specific scenario that was fixed? Just so it's clear to the user what exactly was shipped.
Right now it's pretty cryptic. Especially this part - `This was already possible under specific circumstances, which this PR loosens by expanding the amount of cases such checks can be added in advance.`. I feel that it's very vague.


  The diff is used here as the user can define an ac to cover more flavors than defined in the Resource Groups. In this case if feel more intuitive to add this checks right away since it has to cover any flavor the wl may be assigned. This is supported by the fact that once we get an admission such an AC would in fact be added to the wl no matter the flavor CQ assigned to it.

### Review by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) (commented) — 2026-02-26T10:43:14Z

```diff
@@ -946,6 +946,16 @@ func (c *ClusterQueueWrapper) AdmissionChecks(checks ...kueue.AdmissionCheckRefe
 	return c
 }
 
+// Adds an additional admission check.
+func (c *ClusterQueueWrapper) WithAdmissionCheck(check kueue.AdmissionCheckReference, flavors ...kueue.ResourceFlavorReference) *ClusterQueueWrapper {
+	newRule := kueue.AdmissionCheckStrategyRule{
+		Name:      check,
+		OnFlavors: flavors,
+	}
+	c.Spec.AdmissionChecksStrategy.AdmissionChecks = append(c.Spec.AdmissionChecksStrategy.AdmissionChecks, newRule)
+	return c
+}
```

  There's already an `AdmissionCheckStrategy` function where you can pass `AdmissionCheckStrategyRule`s for the `ClusterQueueWrapper`.
  
  I'd consider re-using that. Right now you are writing sth like this in the tests:
  ```
  ...
  AdmissionChecks("check1", "check2").
  WithAdmissionCheck("check3", kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor2.Name)).
  ...
  ```
  
  Which is not very clear IMO.

  Is the `schdcache.AllFlavors` function relevant anymore? From what I can see, https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/6785 introduced the same function to calculate all flavors 3 times.
  
  [Here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/9feb05e01205ceed50876a9c4e3c03246ade51e1/pkg/util/admissioncheck/admissioncheck.go#L175) it also calculates `allFlavors` in a loop, which is redundant.
  
  Not strictly related to this PR, but we might want a follow-up with a cleanup.

  The allFlavors vs AllFlavors issue is one of dependencies - when trying to clean this code up I encountered a warning abt circular dependencies but was unable to pinpoint which imports were exactly the problem.
  
  In terms of there being two AllFlavors functions - they use different types of "ResourceGroup" - one uses the definition from v1beta2, one a local definition.

```diff
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, additionalFlavor2, true)
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, additionalAc, true)
+		})
+
+		ginkgo.It("should assign the multikueue admission check even before admitted", framework.SlowSpec, func() {
+			jobSet := testingjobset.MakeJobSet("job-set", managerNs.Name).
+				Queue(managerLq.Name).
+				ManagedBy(kueue.MultiKueueControllerName).
+				ReplicatedJobs(
+					testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-1",
+						Replicas:    1,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					}, testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-2",
+						Replicas:    3,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					},
+				).
+				Obj()
+			util.MustCreate(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, jobSet)
+
+			wlLookupKey := types.NamespacedName{Name: workloadjobset.GetWorkloadNameForJobSet(jobSet.Name, jobSet.UID), Namespace: managerNs.Name}
+			ginkgo.By("ensuring multikueue admission check reference is present and in pending state", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdWorkload := &kueue.Workload{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, wlLookupKey, createdWorkload)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					acs := admissioncheck.FindAdmissionCheck(createdWorkload.Status.AdmissionChecks, kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name))
+					g.Expect(acs).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(&kueue.AdmissionCheckState{
+						Name:  kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name),
+						State: kueue.CheckStatePending,
+					}, cmpopts.IgnoreFields(kueue.AdmissionCheckState{}, "LastTransitionTime", "Message", "RetryCount")))
+				}, util.LongTimeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			})
+		})
+
+		ginkgo.It("should keep multikueue admission check reference and properly clean up the remote workload when the connection to an admitting worker is lost", framework.SlowSpec, func() {
+			jobSet := testingjobset.MakeJobSet("job-set", managerNs.Name).
+				Queue(managerLq.Name).
+				ManagedBy(kueue.MultiKueueControllerName).
+				ReplicatedJobs(
+					testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-1",
+						Replicas:    1,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					}, testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-2",
+						Replicas:    3,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					},
+				).
+				Obj()
+			util.MustCreate(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, jobSet)
+
+			wlLookupKey := types.NamespacedName{Name: workloadjobset.GetWorkloadNameForJobSet(jobSet.Name, jobSet.UID), Namespace: managerNs.Name}
+
+			admission := utiltestingapi.MakeAdmission(managerCq.Name).PodSets(
+				kueue.PodSetAssignment{
+					Name: "replicated-job-1",
+					Flavors: map[corev1.ResourceName]kueue.ResourceFlavorReference{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(additionalFlavor1.Name),
+					},
+					ResourceUsage: corev1.ResourceList{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: resource.MustParse("1"),
+					},
+				}, kueue.PodSetAssignment{
+					Name: "replicated-job-2",
+					Flavors: map[corev1.ResourceName]kueue.ResourceFlavorReference{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(additionalFlavor1.Name),
+					},
+					ResourceUsage: corev1.ResourceList{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: resource.MustParse("1"),
+					},
+				},
+			)
+
+			admitWorkloadAndCheckWorkerCopies(multiKueueAC.Name, wlLookupKey, admission)
+
+			var disconnectedTime time.Time
+			ginkgo.By("breaking the connection to worker2", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdCluster := &kueue.MultiKueueCluster{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, client.ObjectKeyFromObject(workerCluster2), createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					createdCluster.Spec.ClusterSource.KubeConfig.Location = "bad-secret"
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Update(managerTestCluster.ctx, createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+				}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdCluster := &kueue.MultiKueueCluster{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, client.ObjectKeyFromObject(workerCluster2), createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					activeCondition := apimeta.FindStatusCondition(createdCluster.Status.Conditions, kueue.MultiKueueClusterActive)
+					g.Expect(activeCondition).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(&metav1.Condition{
+						Type:   kueue.MultiKueueClusterActive,
+						Status: metav1.ConditionFalse,
+						Reason: "BadKubeConfig",
+					}, util.IgnoreConditionMessage, util.IgnoreConditionTimestampsAndObservedGeneration))
+					disconnectedTime = activeCondition.LastTransitionTime.Time
+				}, util.Timeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			})
+
+			ginkgo.By("waiting for quotaReservation to be removed", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdWorkload := &kueue.Workload{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, wlLookupKey, createdWorkload)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					acs := admissioncheck.FindAdmissionCheck(createdWorkload.Status.AdmissionChecks, kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name))
+					// The transition interval should be close to testingKeepReadyTimeout (taking into account the resolution of the LastTransitionTime field)
+					g.Expect(acs.LastTransitionTime.Time).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(disconnectedTime.Add(testingWorkerLostTimeout), cmpopts.EquateApproxTime(2*time.Second)))
+					g.Expect(createdWorkload.Status.Conditions).ToNot(utiltesting.HaveConditionStatusTrue(kueue.WorkloadQuotaReserved))
+				}, util.LongTimeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			})
+
+			ginkgo.By("ensuring multikueue admission check reference is present and in pending state after quota reservation is gone", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdWorkload := &kueue.Workload{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, wlLookupKey, createdWorkload)).To(gomega.Succeed())

+						Name:       kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name),
+						State:      kueue.CheckStatePending,
+						RetryCount: ptr.To(int32(1)),
+					}, cmpopts.IgnoreFields(kueue.AdmissionCheckState{}, "LastTransitionTime", "Message")))
+				}, util.LongTimeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			})
+
+			ginkgo.By("restoring the connection to worker2", func() {
```

  This confused me - I had to go & check that cq.AdmissionChecks specifies all flavors for ACs like the MK one. (I mean, that user-facing API of "no flavors" is internally translated to "all flavors").

### Review by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) (commented) — 2026-03-10T14:41:08Z

- **pkg/workload/admissionchecks.go:167** by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) — 2026-03-10T14:41:07Z
```diff
@@ -158,9 +158,13 @@ func HasAllChecksReady(wl *kueue.Workload) bool {
 	return true
 }
 
-// HasAllChecks returns true if all the mustHaveChecks are present in the workload.
+// HasAllRequiredChecks returns true if all the relevant checks are present in the workload.
 // (They don't have to be in the Ready state; for that, see HasAllChecksReady).
-func HasAllChecks(wl *kueue.Workload, mustHaveChecks sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]) bool {
+func HasAllRequiredChecks(wl *kueue.Workload, allChecks map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference]) bool {
+	admissionFlavors := admissionFlavors(wl.Status.Admission)
+	mustHaveChecks := filterChecks(allChecks, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+		return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+	})
```

  The method differs in that it allows for the wl not to have an admission check. Here - we expect the ac to exist. Due to that difference I decided to keep the two methods separate. On the other hand I saw no point in encapsualting the "filterChecks" call in a separate function (i.e. `checksForAdmission`) as it is only a wrapper that would define the predicate and that seemed like overcomplicating it.


  Yes but that is a differenc cluster queue.
  You are talking about the scheduler cache implementation of the cq.
  This here is the cq object we load from the client. We would have to choose the best place to store it in kueue memory (queue or scheduler cache) and ensure the data is always there and synchronized when performing this in case of the workload controller. I am hesitant to say it is in the scope of this PR as the previous logic also performed the calculation every time.
  
  I can create a followup clean-up-issue if you wish.

  Hmm, what is being tested here?
  
  This essentially duplicates the logic which you've added to `HasAllRequiredAdmissionChecks`.
  I consider this problematic: e.g. when that logic there gets updated, this test will continue to test the _old_ behavior (hardcoded here).
  
  I propose extracting that logic to a common helper method. I mean: `HasAllRequiredAdmissionChecks` should call that helper and then this will become the proper unit test of that helper.

- **test/util/util.go:1389** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-03-10T22:42:19Z
```diff
@@ -1201,6 +1201,64 @@ func IsLoggedEntryAConcurrentModification(le observer.LoggedEntry) bool {
 	return strings.Contains(errorDetals, expectedConcurrentModiciationDetails)
 }
 
+// BreakConnection breaks connection to the cluster, then returns:
+// a callback to restore the connection AND
+// the timestamp of becoming disconnected
+func BreakConnection(ctx context.Context, cli client.Client, cluster *kueue.MultiKueueCluster) (func(), time.Time) {
+	var disconnectedTime time.Time
+	var trueLocation string
+	clusterKey := client.ObjectKeyFromObject(cluster)
+
+	ginkgo.By(fmt.Sprintf("breaking the connection to %s", clusterKey), func() {
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			createdCluster := &kueue.MultiKueueCluster{}
+			g.Expect(cli.Get(ctx, clusterKey, createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+			trueLocation = createdCluster.Spec.ClusterSource.KubeConfig.Location
+			createdCluster.Spec.ClusterSource.KubeConfig.Location = "bad-secret"
+			g.Expect(cli.Update(ctx, createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+		}, Timeout, Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+		gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+			createdCluster := &kueue.MultiKueueCluster{}
+			g.Expect(cli.Get(ctx, clusterKey, createdCluster)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+			activeCondition := apimeta.FindStatusCondition(createdCluster.Status.Conditions, kueue.MultiKueueClusterActive)
+			g.Expect(activeCondition).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(&metav1.Condition{
+				Type:   kueue.MultiKueueClusterActive,
+				Status: metav1.ConditionFalse,
+				Reason: "BadKubeConfig",
+			}, IgnoreConditionMessage, IgnoreConditionTimestampsAndObservedGeneration))
+			disconnectedTime = activeCondition.LastTransitionTime.Time
+		}, Timeout, Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+	})
+
+	return createConnectionRestoringCallback(ctx, cli, cluster, trueLocation), disconnectedTime
+}
+
+func createConnectionRestoringCallback(ctx context.Context, cli client.Client, cluster *kueue.MultiKueueCluster, location string) func() {
```

  Nit: instead of `cluster`, you could pass just `clusterKey`; you seem to need only this.

  I think this sentence parses ambiguously:
  
  * A: ... should get the (ACs that cover all flavors) added
  * B: ... should get the (ACs that cover all (flavors added))

```diff
+			}).Obj(), // todo admitted.Obj(),
```

```diff
+					*utiltestingapi.MakeFlavorQuotas("flavor2").Obj(),
+				).AdmissionCheckStrategy(
+				*utiltestingapi.MakeAdmissionCheckStrategyRule("ac1", "flavor1").Obj(),
+				*utiltestingapi.MakeAdmissionCheckStrategyRule("ac2").Obj(),
+			).Obj(),
+			wantChecks: []kueue.AdmissionCheckState{
+				{
+					Name:  "ac1",
+					State: kueue.CheckStatePending,
+				},
+				{
+					Name:  "ac2",
+					State: kueue.CheckStatePending,
+				},
+			},
+		},
+		"add checks to admitted wl from cq with strategy": {
+			wl: *utiltestingapi.MakeWorkload("wl", "ns").

+					ClusterQueue: "cq",
+					PodSetAssignments: []kueue.PodSetAssignment{

+						},
```

```diff
+// ClusterQueue configuration
+func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, cq *kueue.ClusterQueue) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	log = log.WithValues(
+		"Workload",
+		klog.KObj(wl),
+		"ClusterQueue",
+		klog.KObj(cq),
+	)
+	allChecks := admissioncheck.NewAdmissionChecks(cq)
 
-	// Kueue sets AdmissionChecks first based on ClusterQueue configuration and at this point Workload has no
-	// ResourceFlavors assigned, so we cannot match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavor.
-	// After Quota is reserved, another reconciliation happens and we can match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavors

-		log.V(2).Info("Workload has no Admission", "Workload", klog.KObj(wl))
-		return nil
-	}
+	if wl.Status.Admission != nil {
+		// If we have an admission we can provide all relevant checks right away.
+		// Checks that are defined with an empty list of flavors are considered
+		// to apply to all flavors declared for the ClusterQueue.
+		// These checks are considered valid by this logic, as intended,
+		// because checks with empty OnFlavor lists have their lists populated
+		// with all flavors in the CQ when initially processed by Kueue.
+		return admissionChecksForAdmission(log, allChecks, *wl.Status.Admission)
+	}
+
+	// If no admission is present yet we can only list
+	// the checks which apply to all flavors supported by the ClusterQueue
+	allFlavors := queue.AllFlavors(cq.Spec.ResourceGroups)
+	checksForAllFlavors := filterChecks(allChecks, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+		return allFlavors.Difference(acFlavors).Len() == 0
+	})
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Workload has no Admission: assigning only checks that apply to all workloads in the Cluster Queue regardless of flavor",
+		"Assigned AdmissionChecks",
+		checksForAllFlavors,
+	)
+	return checksForAllFlavors
+}

-		for _, flavor := range podSet.Flavors {
-			assignedFlavors = append(assignedFlavors, flavor)
-		}
+func admissionChecksForAdmission(log logr.Logger, acs map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], admission kueue.Admission) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	admissionFlavors := admissionFlavors(admission)
```

  The local variable admissionFlavors shadows the package-level function name admissionFlavors. While valid in Go, it can be confusing for readers. Consider renaming.

```diff
+	if len(admissionFlavors) > 0 {
+		return filterChecks(acs, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+			return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+		})
```

  In a lot of tests workloads are created with empty requests however.

```diff
 // AdmissionChecksForWorkload returns AdmissionChecks that should be assigned to a specific Workload based on
-// ClusterQueue configuration and ResourceFlavors

-	// If all admissionChecks should be run for all flavors we don't need to wait for Workload's Admission to be set.
-	// This is also the case if admissionChecks are specified with ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionChecks instead of
-	// ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionCheckStrategy
-	hasAllFlavors := true
-	for _, flavors := range admissionChecks {
-		if !flavors.Equal(allFlavors) {
-			hasAllFlavors = false
-		}
-	}
-	if hasAllFlavors {
-		return sets.New(slices.Collect(maps.Keys(admissionChecks))...)
-	}
+// ClusterQueue configuration
+func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, cq *kueue.ClusterQueue) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	log = log.WithValues(
+		"Workload",
+		klog.KObj(wl),
+		"ClusterQueue",
+		klog.KObj(cq),
+	)
+	allChecks := admissioncheck.NewAdmissionChecks(cq)
 
-	// Kueue sets AdmissionChecks first based on ClusterQueue configuration and at this point Workload has no
-	// ResourceFlavors assigned, so we cannot match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavor.
-	// After Quota is reserved, another reconciliation happens and we can match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavors
-	if wl.Status.Admission == nil {
-		log.V(2).Info("Workload has no Admission", "Workload", klog.KObj(wl))
-		return nil
-	}
+	if wl.Status.Admission != nil {
+		// If we have an admission we can provide all relevant checks right away.
+		// Checks that are defined with an empty list of flavors are considered
+		// to apply to all flavors declared for the ClusterQueue.
+		// These checks are considered valid by this logic, as intended,
+		// because checks with empty OnFlavor lists have their lists populated
+		// with all flavors in the CQ when initially processed by Kueue.
+		return admissionChecksForAdmission(log, allChecks, *wl.Status.Admission)
+	}
+
+	// If no admission is present yet we can only list
+	// the checks which apply to all flavors supported by the ClusterQueue
+	allFlavors := queue.AllFlavors(cq.Spec.ResourceGroups)
+	checksForAllFlavors := filterChecks(allChecks, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+		return acFlavors.IsSuperset(allFlavors)
+	})
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Workload has no Admission: assigning only checks that apply to all workloads in the Cluster Queue regardless of flavor",
+		"Assigned AdmissionChecks",
+		checksForAllFlavors,
+	)
+	return checksForAllFlavors
+}
 
-	var assignedFlavors []kueue.ResourceFlavorReference
-	for _, podSet := range wl.Status.Admission.PodSetAssignments {
-		for _, flavor := range podSet.Flavors {
-			assignedFlavors = append(assignedFlavors, flavor)
-		}
+func admissionChecksForAdmission(log logr.Logger, acs map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], admission kueue.Admission) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	admissionFlavors := findAdmissionFlavors(admission)
+	if len(admissionFlavors) > 0 {
+		return filterChecks(acs, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+			return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+		})
 	}
 
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Admission has no Flavors; assigning all checks",
+		"AdmissionChecks",
+		acs,
+	)
+	return sets.KeySet(acs)
```

  Is this logic change necessary? Looking at the OG code, if there are no assigned flavors the assigned ACs would be empty. This is slightly more intuitive to me.

```diff
+		// because checks with empty OnFlavor lists have their lists populated
+		// with all flavors in the CQ when initially processed by Kueue.
+		return admissionChecksForAdmission(log, allChecks, *wl.Status.Admission)
+	}

+func admissionChecksForAdmission(log logr.Logger, acs map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], admission kueue.Admission) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	admissionFlavors := findAdmissionFlavors(admission)
+	if len(admissionFlavors) > 0 {
+		return filterChecks(acs, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+			return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+		})
 	}

+		acs,

```

  OG code logic would assign either:
  1. All checks if all covered all flavors in the CQ.
  2. No flavors otherwise.
  
  I opted to make it "Assign all flavors always" for 2 reasons:
  1. Existing tests that don't bother assigning flavors all expect all defined ACs (if any defined that is) to be applied.
  2. It seems a safer default - we expect a flavor to be there - if it isn't it seems safer to force all checks onto it instead of letting it pass without issue. This way if a test defines checks and expects only some to apply, but the test author forgets to assign flavors, they will see their workload not admitted as unexpected checks block it, instead of being admitted due to no checks blocking, potentially producing a false positive.

  If the OG code logic did not assign any checks in case 2 (I assume you meant "checks" not "flavors"), then how do existing tests expect all defined ACs to be applied?
  > Existing tests that don't bother assigning flavors all expect all defined ACs (if any defined that is) to be applied.
  
  Wouldn't those tests fail?
  
  Since this is an "impossible" scenario, it feels unintuitive to me to handle it this way and having tests rely on this behavior instead of making them perform the correct setup. When I read this logic now, I think "ok, so there is a scenario where an admission has no flavors". I think some explanation is missing in the code at the very least.

  Beacause all existing tests that define checks but don't define flavors (or rather don't define resource requests for test workloads) create the checks with default flavors, meaning all checks cover all flavors and, in the past, had fallen into that category. There was only one exception to the rule which I have amended.
  
  If we want to remove this logic and ensure the test setups are correct - i would say it is a good idea but it should be left to a followup that sweeps across all tests and corrects them. The change could be potentially significant and deserves its own issue for it. I can create the follow up issue describing the problem - lmk if that is to your satisfaction.
  
  TL;DR - i agree with your point that it would be better to fix test setups, but that is too big a change to be a drive-by cleanup, and should be addressed in a followup cleanup-issue.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-04-07T12:37:44Z

```diff
+			gomega.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Create(managerTestCluster.ctx, flavor2)).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+			additionalAc = utiltestingapi.MakeAdmissionCheck("non-mk-ac").
+				ControllerName(kueue.MultiKueueControllerName).
+				Obj()
+			util.MustCreate(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, additionalAc)
+			util.SetAdmissionCheckActive(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, additionalAc, metav1.ConditionTrue)
+
+			flavor1Quotas := *utiltestingapi.MakeFlavorQuotas(flavor1.Name).Resource(corev1.ResourceCPU, "10").Obj()
+			flavor2Quotas := *utiltestingapi.MakeFlavorQuotas(flavor2.Name).Resource(corev1.ResourceMemory, "100Gi").Obj()
+			resourceGroups := []kueue.ResourceGroup{
+				utiltestingapi.ResourceGroup(flavor1Quotas),
+				utiltestingapi.ResourceGroup(flavor2Quotas),
+			}
+
+			rule1 := *utiltestingapi.MakeAdmissionCheckStrategyRule(
+				kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name),
+				kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor1.Name),
+				kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor2.Name),
+			).Obj()
+			rule2 := *utiltestingapi.MakeAdmissionCheckStrategyRule(
+				kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(additionalAc.Name),
+				kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor2.Name),
+			).Obj()
+			acRules := []kueue.AdmissionCheckStrategyRule{
+				rule1,
+				rule2,
+			}
+
+			gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+				k8sClient := managerTestCluster.client
+				ctx := managerTestCluster.ctx
+				updatedCq := &kueue.ClusterQueue{}
+				gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Get(ctx, client.ObjectKeyFromObject(managerCq), updatedCq)).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+
+				updatedCq.Spec.ResourceGroups = resourceGroups
+				updatedCq.Spec.AdmissionChecksStrategy = &kueue.AdmissionChecksStrategy{
+					AdmissionChecks: acRules,
+				}
+				gomega.Expect(k8sClient.Update(ctx, updatedCq)).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			}, util.LongTimeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+		})
+
+		ginkgo.AfterEach(func() {
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, managerCq, true)
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, flavor1, true)
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, flavor2, true)
+			util.ExpectObjectToBeDeleted(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, additionalAc, true)
+		})
+
+		ginkgo.It("should assign the multikueue admission check even before admitted", framework.SlowSpec, func() {
+			jobSet := testingjobset.MakeJobSet("job-set", managerNs.Name).
+				Queue(managerLq.Name).
+				ManagedBy(kueue.MultiKueueControllerName).
+				ReplicatedJobs(
+					testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-1",
+						Replicas:    1,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					}, testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-2",
+						Replicas:    3,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					},
+				).
+				Obj()
+			util.MustCreate(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, jobSet)
+
+			wlLookupKey := types.NamespacedName{Name: workloadjobset.GetWorkloadNameForJobSet(jobSet.Name, jobSet.UID), Namespace: managerNs.Name}
+			ginkgo.By("ensuring multikueue admission check reference is present and in pending state", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdWorkload := &kueue.Workload{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, wlLookupKey, createdWorkload)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					acs := admissioncheck.FindAdmissionCheck(createdWorkload.Status.AdmissionChecks, kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name))
+					g.Expect(acs).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(&kueue.AdmissionCheckState{
+						Name:  kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name),
+						State: kueue.CheckStatePending,
+					}, cmpopts.IgnoreFields(kueue.AdmissionCheckState{}, "LastTransitionTime", "Message", "RetryCount")))
+				}, util.LongTimeout, util.Interval).Should(gomega.Succeed())
+			})
+		})
+
+		ginkgo.It("should keep multikueue admission check reference and properly clean up the remote workload when the connection to an admitting worker is lost", framework.SlowSpec, func() {
+			jobSet := testingjobset.MakeJobSet("job-set", managerNs.Name).
+				Queue(managerLq.Name).
+				ManagedBy(kueue.MultiKueueControllerName).
+				ReplicatedJobs(
+					testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-1",
+						Replicas:    1,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					}, testingjobset.ReplicatedJobRequirements{
+						Name:        "replicated-job-2",
+						Replicas:    3,
+						Parallelism: 1,
+						Completions: 1,
+					},
+				).
+				Obj()
+			util.MustCreate(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, jobSet)
+
+			wlLookupKey := types.NamespacedName{Name: workloadjobset.GetWorkloadNameForJobSet(jobSet.Name, jobSet.UID), Namespace: managerNs.Name}
+
+			admission := utiltestingapi.MakeAdmission(managerCq.Name).PodSets(
+				kueue.PodSetAssignment{
+					Name: "replicated-job-1",
+					Flavors: map[corev1.ResourceName]kueue.ResourceFlavorReference{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor1.Name),
+					},
+					ResourceUsage: corev1.ResourceList{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: resource.MustParse("1"),
+					},
+				}, kueue.PodSetAssignment{
+					Name: "replicated-job-2",
+					Flavors: map[corev1.ResourceName]kueue.ResourceFlavorReference{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: kueue.ResourceFlavorReference(flavor1.Name),
+					},
+					ResourceUsage: corev1.ResourceList{
+						corev1.ResourceCPU: resource.MustParse("1"),
+					},
+				},
+			)
+
+			admitWorkloadAndCheckWorkerCopies(multiKueueAC.Name, wlLookupKey, admission)
+
+			restoreConnectionToWorker2, disconnectedTime := util.BreakConnection(managerTestCluster.ctx, managerTestCluster.client, workerCluster2)
+
+			ginkgo.By("waiting for quotaReservation to be removed", func() {
+				gomega.Eventually(func(g gomega.Gomega) {
+					createdWorkload := &kueue.Workload{}
+					g.Expect(managerTestCluster.client.Get(managerTestCluster.ctx, wlLookupKey, createdWorkload)).To(gomega.Succeed())
+					acs := admissioncheck.FindAdmissionCheck(createdWorkload.Status.AdmissionChecks, kueue.AdmissionCheckReference(multiKueueAC.Name))
+					// The transition interval should be close to testingKeepReadyTimeout (taking into account the resolution of the LastTransitionTime field)
+					g.Expect(acs.LastTransitionTime.Time).To(gomega.BeComparableTo(disconnectedTime.Add(testingWorkerLostTimeout), cmpopts.EquateApproxTime(2*time.Second)))
```

  Is checking the LastTransitionTime anyhow relevant here? It does not feel like responsibility of the PR really.


  The thing is the test faces a race condition without this refactor - the effect should be the same but the way the test is written it may not be fast enough to catch the window when the workload is evicted. The tests then fails because the assertion was not fast enough. Now the tests verifies the stable state after the eviction is processed: once the MG workload backs off, the remotes are cleaned up and the MW is re-scheduled, gets the reservation back and is pending on the remotes.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-04-07T13:15:11Z

- **pkg/workload/workload.go:1549** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-04-07T13:15:11Z
```diff
@@ -1498,48 +1499,79 @@ func RemoveFinalizer(ctx context.Context, c client.Client, wl *kueue.Workload) e
 	return nil
 }
 
+type flavorSet = sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference]
+
 // AdmissionChecksForWorkload returns AdmissionChecks that should be assigned to a specific Workload based on
-// ClusterQueue configuration and ResourceFlavors
-func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, admissionChecks map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], allFlavors sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference]) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
-	// If all admissionChecks should be run for all flavors we don't need to wait for Workload's Admission to be set.
-	// This is also the case if admissionChecks are specified with ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionChecks instead of
-	// ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionCheckStrategy
-	hasAllFlavors := true
-	for _, flavors := range admissionChecks {
-		if !flavors.Equal(allFlavors) {
-			hasAllFlavors = false
-		}
-	}
-	if hasAllFlavors {
-		return sets.New(slices.Collect(maps.Keys(admissionChecks))...)
-	}
+// ClusterQueue configuration
+func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, cq *kueue.ClusterQueue) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	log = log.WithValues(
+		"Workload",
+		klog.KObj(wl),
+		"ClusterQueue",
+		klog.KObj(cq),
+	)
+	allChecks := admissioncheck.NewAdmissionChecks(cq)
 
-	// Kueue sets AdmissionChecks first based on ClusterQueue configuration and at this point Workload has no
-	// ResourceFlavors assigned, so we cannot match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavor.
-	// After Quota is reserved, another reconciliation happens and we can match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavors
-	if wl.Status.Admission == nil {
-		log.V(2).Info("Workload has no Admission", "Workload", klog.KObj(wl))
-		return nil
-	}
+	if wl.Status.Admission != nil {
+		// If we have an admission we can provide all relevant checks right away.
+		// Checks that are defined with an empty list of flavors are considered
+		// to apply to all flavors declared for the ClusterQueue.
+		// These checks are considered valid by this logic, as intended,
+		// because checks with empty OnFlavor lists have their lists populated
+		// with all flavors in the CQ when initially processed by Kueue.
+		return admissionChecksForAdmission(log, allChecks, *wl.Status.Admission)
+	}
+
+	// If no admission is present yet we can only list
+	// the checks which apply to all flavors supported by the ClusterQueue
+	allFlavors := queue.AllFlavors(cq.Spec.ResourceGroups)
+	checksForAllFlavors := filterChecks(allChecks, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+		return acFlavors.IsSuperset(allFlavors)
+	})
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Workload has no Admission: assigning only checks that apply to all workloads in the Cluster Queue regardless of flavor",
+		"Assigned AdmissionChecks",
+		checksForAllFlavors,
+	)
+	return checksForAllFlavors
+}
 
-	var assignedFlavors []kueue.ResourceFlavorReference
-	for _, podSet := range wl.Status.Admission.PodSetAssignments {
-		for _, flavor := range podSet.Flavors {
-			assignedFlavors = append(assignedFlavors, flavor)
-		}
+func admissionChecksForAdmission(log logr.Logger, acs map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], admission kueue.Admission) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	admissionFlavors := findAdmissionFlavors(admission)
+	if len(admissionFlavors) > 0 {
+		return filterChecks(acs, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+			return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+		})
 	}
 
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Admission has no Flavors; assigning all checks",
+		"AdmissionChecks",
+		acs,
+	)
+	return sets.KeySet(acs)
```

  Why don't we just return `findAdmissionFlavors` here? Are there any integration or e2e tests fail if we do that? I'm wondering maybe there is some weird unit tests only which led you to set the code like that.


  When the admission had no flavors, we returned:
  * no admission checks when any admission check didn't cover any of the flavors defined for the CQ,
  * all admission checks when all of them covered all flavors of the CQ.
  
  Most tests I encountered that did not bother to assign flavors to the admission, rely on the latter behavior.
  
  After my change, an admission with no flavors is expected to fulfill all ACs. 
  This seemed like the better option as it allows the existing tests to keep working according to their assumptions, without exposing us to always allowing workloads with no flavors to be admitted immediately (instead they have to comply with a superset of admission checks any legal flavor would be assigned).
  
  While less dangerous, I don't like this being allowed to happen. As such I propose creating a follow up to ensure all tests set up flavors properly. This is too big a task for a drive-by cleanup. If necessary, the task can be separately implemented before to make sure we don't have to verify this test-specific behavior.

  > TL;DR - i agree with your point that it would be better to fix test setups, but that is too big a change to be a drive-by cleanup, and should be addressed in a followup cleanup-issue.
  
  I would still like to know if this is just about unit tests or integration / e2e too, and how many. Sure, adjusting tests is a toil but changing behavior as a drive-by is also tricky. 
  
  As this PR is fixing a bug I would like to consider for cherrypicked. As such, any drive by changes, even to seemingly unimportant scenarios requires more care when reviewing.

```diff
+		"Admission has no Flavors; assigning all checks",
+		"AdmissionChecks",
+		acs,
+	)
+	return sets.KeySet(acs)
```

  Number of tests that fail without this special clause:
  * 4 Unit Tests.
  * 3 Integration Tests.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-04-07T14:29:48Z

- **pkg/workload/workload.go:1549** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-04-07T14:29:47Z
```diff
@@ -1498,48 +1499,79 @@ func RemoveFinalizer(ctx context.Context, c client.Client, wl *kueue.Workload) e
 	return nil
 }
 
+type flavorSet = sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference]
+
 // AdmissionChecksForWorkload returns AdmissionChecks that should be assigned to a specific Workload based on
-// ClusterQueue configuration and ResourceFlavors
-func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, admissionChecks map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], allFlavors sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference]) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
-	// If all admissionChecks should be run for all flavors we don't need to wait for Workload's Admission to be set.
-	// This is also the case if admissionChecks are specified with ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionChecks instead of
-	// ClusterQueue.Spec.AdmissionCheckStrategy
-	hasAllFlavors := true
-	for _, flavors := range admissionChecks {
-		if !flavors.Equal(allFlavors) {
-			hasAllFlavors = false
-		}
-	}
-	if hasAllFlavors {
-		return sets.New(slices.Collect(maps.Keys(admissionChecks))...)
-	}
+// ClusterQueue configuration
+func AdmissionChecksForWorkload(log logr.Logger, wl *kueue.Workload, cq *kueue.ClusterQueue) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	log = log.WithValues(
+		"Workload",
+		klog.KObj(wl),
+		"ClusterQueue",
+		klog.KObj(cq),
+	)
+	allChecks := admissioncheck.NewAdmissionChecks(cq)
 
-	// Kueue sets AdmissionChecks first based on ClusterQueue configuration and at this point Workload has no
-	// ResourceFlavors assigned, so we cannot match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavor.
-	// After Quota is reserved, another reconciliation happens and we can match AdmissionChecks to ResourceFlavors
-	if wl.Status.Admission == nil {
-		log.V(2).Info("Workload has no Admission", "Workload", klog.KObj(wl))
-		return nil
-	}
+	if wl.Status.Admission != nil {
+		// If we have an admission we can provide all relevant checks right away.
+		// Checks that are defined with an empty list of flavors are considered
+		// to apply to all flavors declared for the ClusterQueue.
+		// These checks are considered valid by this logic, as intended,
+		// because checks with empty OnFlavor lists have their lists populated
+		// with all flavors in the CQ when initially processed by Kueue.
+		return admissionChecksForAdmission(log, allChecks, *wl.Status.Admission)
+	}
+
+	// If no admission is present yet we can only list
+	// the checks which apply to all flavors supported by the ClusterQueue
+	allFlavors := queue.AllFlavors(cq.Spec.ResourceGroups)
+	checksForAllFlavors := filterChecks(allChecks, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+		return acFlavors.IsSuperset(allFlavors)
+	})
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Workload has no Admission: assigning only checks that apply to all workloads in the Cluster Queue regardless of flavor",
+		"Assigned AdmissionChecks",
+		checksForAllFlavors,
+	)
+	return checksForAllFlavors
+}
 
-	var assignedFlavors []kueue.ResourceFlavorReference
-	for _, podSet := range wl.Status.Admission.PodSetAssignments {
-		for _, flavor := range podSet.Flavors {
-			assignedFlavors = append(assignedFlavors, flavor)
-		}
+func admissionChecksForAdmission(log logr.Logger, acs map[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference]sets.Set[kueue.ResourceFlavorReference], admission kueue.Admission) sets.Set[kueue.AdmissionCheckReference] {
+	admissionFlavors := findAdmissionFlavors(admission)
+	if len(admissionFlavors) > 0 {
+		return filterChecks(acs, func(acFlavors flavorSet) bool {
+			return admissionFlavors.Intersection(acFlavors).Len() > 0
+		})
 	}
 
+	log.V(3).Info(
+		"Admission has no Flavors; assigning all checks",
+		"AdmissionChecks",
+		acs,
+	)
+	return sets.KeySet(acs)
```

  Ok, thanks for explaining that difference in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/9359/changes#r3045285324
  
  I think the previous behavior was very spooky anyway, not not something we would like to maintain:
  ```
  * no admission checks when any admission check didn't cover any of the flavors defined for the CQ,
  * all admission checks when all of them covered all flavors of the CQ.
  ```
  So, I think I'm ok with the new "all admission checks" for this case.
